==============================================================================
Set 1 | Q.No 21 | Topic: Polity & Constitution | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Which body recommends the distribution of taxes between Center and States?
   A) Planning Commission
   B) Finance Commission  <-- CORRECT
   C) Parliament
   D) NITI Aayog
Answer: B
Why correct: The Finance Commission, a constitutional body under Article 280, is constituted every five years by the President to recommend how the net proceeds of taxes should be divided (vertical devolution) between the Union and the States, and how funds should be distributed among the States (horizontal devolution).
Why A is wrong: The Planning Commission (1950-2014) prepared Five-Year Plans and allocated plan assistance, but it had no role in dividing tax revenue and is now defunct.
Why C is wrong: Parliament enacts tax laws and passes the Budget, but it does not recommend the formula for sharing tax proceeds with the States.
Why D is wrong: NITI Aayog is only an advisory think-tank that replaced the Planning Commission; it has no constitutional power over tax devolution.
Note: The 15th Finance Commission (chaired by N.K. Singh) recommended a 41% share of the divisible pool for the States.

==============================================================================
Set 1 | Q.No 22 | Topic: Polity & Constitution | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Who appoints the chairman and members of the Finance Commission?
   A) Parliament
   B) Union Cabinet
   C) President  <-- CORRECT
   D) Prime Minister
Answer: C
Why correct: Under Article 280, the President of India constitutes the Finance Commission and appoints its Chairman and the other members, along with deciding their qualifications and manner of selection.
Why A is wrong: Parliament only enacts the law laying down qualifications of members; it does not appoint them.
Why B is wrong: The Union Cabinet may advise the President, but the formal appointing authority is the President.
Why D is wrong: The Prime Minister heads the Council of Ministers but does not appoint the Finance Commission.
Note: A Finance Commission has a Chairman and four other members.

Set 1 | Q.No 23 | Topic: Art & Culture | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: During which festival is Gaur dance predominantly performed?
   A) Diwali
   B) Holi  <-- CORRECT
   C) Navratri
   D) Baisakhi
Answer: B
Why correct: The Gaur (bison-horn) dance is a tribal dance of the Maria Gonds of the Bastar region (Chhattisgarh/Madhya Pradesh) and is performed prominently during festive/spring celebrations associated with Holi.
Why A is wrong: Diwali is the festival of lights celebrated with lamps and fireworks, not specifically with the Gaur dance.
Why C is wrong: Navratri is associated with Garba and Dandiya of Gujarat, not the Gaur dance.
Why D is wrong: Baisakhi is a Punjabi harvest festival celebrated with the Bhangra and Gidda dances.
Note: Dancers wear headdresses made of bison (gaur) horns, which gives the dance its name.

Set 1 | Q.No 24 | Topic: Art & Culture | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Which Sikh scripture is recited during Hola Mohalla?
   A) Guru Granth Sahib  <-- CORRECT
   B) Bhagavad Gita
   C) Quran
   D) Bible
Answer: A
Why correct: Hola Mohalla is a Sikh festival started by Guru Gobind Singh; the Guru Granth Sahib, the holy scripture of the Sikhs, is recited during its religious observances.
Why B is wrong: The Bhagavad Gita is a Hindu scripture, part of the Mahabharata, not recited at Hola Mohalla.
Why C is wrong: The Quran is the holy book of Islam.
Why D is wrong: The Bible is the holy book of Christianity.
Note: Hola Mohalla is celebrated at Anandpur Sahib a day after Holi and features mock battles and martial-arts (Gatka) displays by the Nihangs.

Set 1 | Q.No 25 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: When is acceleration considered positive?
   A) When it is opposite to velocity
   B) When velocity is decreasing
   C) When it is in the direction of velocity  <-- CORRECT
   D) When the object is at rest
Answer: C
Why correct: Acceleration is taken as positive when it acts in the same direction as the velocity, because the body then speeds up in its direction of motion.
Why A is wrong: When acceleration is opposite to velocity it is negative acceleration (retardation/deceleration).
Why B is wrong: Decreasing velocity means the acceleration opposes motion, i.e. it is negative.
Why D is wrong: An object at rest with no change in velocity has zero acceleration.
Note: Acceleration is a vector quantity, so its sign depends on the chosen positive direction relative to the velocity.

Set 1 | Q.No 26 | Topic: Books & Authors | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Frankenstein is written by :
   A) Mary Shelley  <-- CORRECT
   B) Bram Stoker
   C) H.G. Wells
   D) Robert Louis Stevenson
Answer: A
Why correct: Frankenstein; or, The Modern Prometheus (1818) was written by the English author Mary Shelley.
Why B is wrong: Bram Stoker wrote Dracula (1897).
Why C is wrong: H.G. Wells wrote science-fiction classics such as The Time Machine and The War of the Worlds.
Why D is wrong: Robert Louis Stevenson wrote Treasure Island and Strange Case of Dr Jekyll and Mr Hyde.
Note: Mary Shelley wrote Frankenstein at the age of 18-19; it is often considered the first true science-fiction novel.

Set 1 | Q.No 27 | Topic: Economy | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: The Ease of Doing Business (EODB) indicator “Enforcing Contracts” measures:
   A) implementation of labor regulations
   B) Ease of paying and managing taxes
   C) Efficiency of the judicial system in resolving commercial disputes  <-- CORRECT
   D) Effectiveness of law enforcement agencies
Answer: C
Why correct: In the World Bank's Ease of Doing Business framework, the 'Enforcing Contracts' indicator measures the time, cost and procedural quality of the judicial system in resolving a standardised commercial dispute.
Why A is wrong: Labour-regulation implementation is captured by separate labour-market indicators, not Enforcing Contracts.
Why B is wrong: Ease of paying and managing taxes is measured by the 'Paying Taxes' indicator.
Why D is wrong: Effectiveness of law-enforcement (police) agencies is a governance/security measure, not part of this EODB indicator.
Note: The World Bank discontinued the Doing Business report in 2021 and is replacing it with the Business Ready (B-READY) project.

Set 1 | Q.No 28 | Topic: Sports | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: In which city and year were the first World Athletics Championships held?
   A) Helsinki, 1983  <-- CORRECT
   B) Tokyo, 1991
   C) Rome, 1987
   D) Berlin, 1993
Answer: A
Why correct: The first World Athletics Championships were held in Helsinki, Finland, in 1983.
Why B is wrong: Tokyo hosted the 1991 edition (and again in 2007).
Why C is wrong: Rome hosted the 1987 World Championships.
Why D is wrong: The 1993 Championships were held in Stuttgart, not Berlin (Berlin hosted in 2009).
Note: Helsinki's Olympic Stadium, which hosted the 1952 Olympics, was the venue for the inaugural 1983 Championships.

Set 1 | Q.No 29 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: if a spacecraft travels at 30 km/s, how long will it take to cover 1 AU (150 million km)?
   A) 15 days
   B) 58 days  <-- CORRECT
   C) 100 days
   D) 365 days
Answer: B
Why correct: Time = distance / speed = 150,000,000 km / 30 km/s = 5,000,000 seconds, which is about 57.9 days, i.e. roughly 58 days.
Why A is wrong: 15 days would require a speed of about 116 km/s.
Why C is wrong: 100 days corresponds to roughly 17 km/s.
Why D is wrong: 365 days (one year) corresponds to a speed of under 5 km/s.
Note: 1 AU is the average Earth-Sun distance; light covers it in about 8 minutes 20 seconds.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: in which year did India take over the BRICS Chairship from Russia?
   A) 2020
   B) 2021  <-- CORRECT
   C) 2022
   D) 2023
Answer: B
Why correct: India assumed the BRICS Chairship in 2021, hosting the 13th BRICS Summit virtually that year.
Why A is wrong: In 2020 Russia held the BRICS Chair.
Why C is wrong: China chaired BRICS in 2022.
Why D is wrong: South Africa chaired BRICS in 2023.
Note: BRICS originally stood for Brazil, Russia, India, China and South Africa; it expanded with new members from 2024.

Set 1 | Q.No 31 | Topic: Economy | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: What was the main drawback of small-scale industry reservation policies?
   A) They encouraged monopoly power
   B) They eliminated export opportunities
   C) They excluded rural entrepreneurs
   D) They restricted economies of scale and technological upgrading  <-- CORRECT
Answer: D
Why correct: Reserving products exclusively for small-scale industries kept firms artificially small, which restricted economies of scale and discouraged investment in modern technology, hurting productivity and competitiveness.
Why A is wrong: The policy was meant to prevent monopoly by protecting small firms, not to encourage monopoly power.
Why B is wrong: It did not specifically eliminate export opportunities; the core problem was scale and technology.
Why C is wrong: Reservation did not exclude rural entrepreneurs; in fact small units were widely spread.
Note: India progressively 'de-reserved' SSI products after 1997, and the reservation list was abolished entirely by 2015.

Set 1 | Q.No 32 | Topic: Economy | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Which was the model for the First Five-Year Plan (1951-1956)?
   A) Solow model
   B) Harrod-Domar model  <-- CORRECT
   C) Keynesian model
   D) Mahalanobis model
Answer: B
Why correct: India's First Five-Year Plan (1951-56) was based on the Harrod-Domar model, which links growth to the rate of saving and investment and the capital-output ratio.
Why A is wrong: The Solow growth model came later and was not the basis of the First Plan.
Why C is wrong: The Keynesian model focuses on demand management, not the planning framework used here.
Why D is wrong: The Mahalanobis model was the basis of the Second Five-Year Plan (1956-61), not the First.
Note: The First Plan prioritised agriculture and irrigation following the disruptions of Partition.

Set 1 | Q.No 33 | Topic: Sports | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: What is the length of a standard field hockey pitch?
   A) 80 m
   B) 91.4 m  <-- CORRECT
   C) 100 m
   D) 105m
Answer: B
Why correct: A standard field-hockey pitch is 91.4 metres long (100 yards) and 55 metres wide.
Why A is wrong: 80 m is shorter than the regulation length.
Why C is wrong: 100 m is the length of a standard football pitch's playing area, not a hockey pitch.
Why D is wrong: 105 m is the typical length of a full-size football (soccer) field.
Note: The dimensions come from the old imperial measure of 100 yards by 60 yards.

Set 1 | Q.No 34 | Topic: Schemes & Government | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: What is the goal of the Atal Mission for Rejuvenation and Urban Transformation (AMRUT) scheme launched in 2015?
   A) Promote digital services
   B) Expand rural employment
   C) Enhance agricultural marketing
   D) Urban infrastructure and water supply  <-- CORRECT
Answer: D
Why correct: AMRUT, launched in 2015, aims to provide basic urban infrastructure - especially assured water supply, sewerage, drainage and green spaces - in selected cities and towns.
Why A is wrong: Promoting digital services is the focus of Digital India, not AMRUT.
Why B is wrong: Expanding rural employment is the goal of MGNREGA.
Why C is wrong: Agricultural marketing is addressed by schemes like e-NAM, not AMRUT.
Note: AMRUT 2.0 was launched in 2021 with the goal of universal water-supply coverage in all statutory towns.

Set 1 | Q.No 35 | Topic: Economy | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Which financial institution plays the lead role in supporting India’s export and import activities?
   A) NABARD
   B) EXIM Bank  <-- CORRECT
   C) World Bank
   D) SIDBI
Answer: B
Why correct: The Export-Import (EXIM) Bank of India is the apex financial institution set up in 1982 specifically to finance and promote India's foreign trade.
Why A is wrong: NABARD is the apex bank for agriculture and rural development.
Why C is wrong: The World Bank is an international multilateral lender, not India's export-import bank.
Why D is wrong: SIDBI is the principal institution for financing small and medium enterprises.
Note: EXIM Bank also extends Lines of Credit on behalf of the Government of India to other developing countries.

Set 1 | Q.No 36 | Topic: History | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Who mentioned the role of the Banjaras in transporting grain in his memoirs?
   A) Babur
   B) Humayun
   C) Sher Shah Suri
   D) Jahangir  <-- CORRECT
Answer: D
Why correct: Emperor Jahangir, in his memoirs (the Tuzuk-i-Jahangiri / Jahangirnama), described the Banjaras as itinerant traders who transported grain on bullocks across the country.
Why A is wrong: Babur's memoirs (Baburnama) focus on his conquests and observations of India, not the Banjaras' grain trade.
Why B is wrong: Humayun did not leave such memoirs; his life was recorded by others (e.g. the Humayun-nama by Gulbadan Begum).
Why C is wrong: Sher Shah Suri is known for administrative reforms and the Grand Trunk Road, not for memoirs on the Banjaras.
Note: The Banjaras were a mobile trading community who moved goods in large caravans called 'tandas'.

Set 1 | Q.No 37 | Topic: History | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: What term was used to describe the student stage of life in early Hindu philosophy?
   A) Vanaprastha
   B) Brahmachari  <-- CORRECT
   C) Sannyasin
   D) Grihastha
Answer: B
Why correct: In the ancient Hindu ashrama system, 'Brahmacharya' was the first stage of life - the celibate student stage devoted to learning under a guru. A student was called a Brahmachari.
Why A is wrong: Vanaprastha is the third stage - gradual retirement and withdrawal from worldly life.
Why C is wrong: Sannyasin refers to the fourth stage - renunciation of all worldly attachments.
Why D is wrong: Grihastha is the second stage - the householder/family life.
Note: The four ashramas are Brahmacharya, Grihastha, Vanaprastha and Sannyasa.

Set 1 | Q.No 38 | Topic: Economy | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: As per a report by Prime Minister’s Economic Advisory Panel EAC-PM, the number of domestic migrants have lowered by nearly between 2011 and 2023.
   A) 12%  <-- CORRECT
   B) 9%
   C) 15%
   D) 21%
Answer: A
Why correct: According to the EAC-PM (Economic Advisory Council to the Prime Minister) analysis, domestic migration fell by nearly 12% between 2011 and 2023, indicating greater local economic opportunity.
Why B is wrong: 9% understates the decline reported.
Why C is wrong: 15% is higher than the figure cited in the report.
Why D is wrong: 21% overstates the reported fall in migration.
Note: The EAC-PM is a non-constitutional advisory body that gives the Prime Minister independent economic advice.

Set 1 | Q.No 39 | Topic: Polity & Constitution | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: The PCPNDT Act was enacted by the Government of India in for prohibition of sex selection.
   A) 1991
   B) 1994  <-- CORRECT
   C) 2011
   D) 2015
Answer: B
Why correct: The Pre-Conception and Pre-Natal Diagnostic Techniques (PCPNDT) Act was enacted in 1994 to prohibit sex selection and the misuse of diagnostic techniques for determining the sex of a foetus.
Why A is wrong: 1991 is incorrect; the Act came three years later.
Why C is wrong: 2011 was the year of a Census that highlighted the skewed child sex ratio, not the year of the Act.
Why D is wrong: 2015 is much later; major amendments to the Act were made in 2003, not 2015.
Note: The Act was significantly amended in 2003 to also regulate pre-conception sex-selection techniques.

Set 1 | Q.No 40 | Topic: History | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: To whom did the rebel soldiers of the Meerut Regiment want to hand over the rule of the country?
   A) Bahadur Shah Zafar  <-- CORRECT
   B) Peshwa Baji Rao Il
   C) Nana Saheb
   D) Rani Lakshmibai
Answer: A
Why correct: The rebel sepoys of the Meerut regiment marched to Delhi in May 1857 and proclaimed the aged Mughal emperor Bahadur Shah Zafar II as the symbolic ruler of Hindustan.
Why B is wrong: Peshwa Baji Rao II had died in 1851; it was his adopted heir Nana Saheb who led the revolt at Kanpur.
Why C is wrong: Nana Saheb led the rebellion in Kanpur, but the Meerut sepoys went to Delhi to the Mughal emperor.
Why D is wrong: Rani Lakshmibai led the revolt at Jhansi, not the figure the Meerut soldiers turned to.
Note: After the revolt was crushed, Bahadur Shah Zafar was exiled to Rangoon, where he died in 1862.

Set 2 | Q.No 21 | Topic: Polity & Constitution | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: केंद्रीय मंत्रिपरिषद में मंत्रियों की अधिकतम संख्या निम्नलिखित तक सीमित है:
   A) 10% of the Lok Sabha
   B) 12% of the Lok Sabha
   C) 15% of the Lok Sabha  <-- CORRECT
   D) 20% of the Lok Sabha
Answer: C
Why correct: The 91st Constitutional Amendment (2003) inserted Article 75(1A), capping the total number of ministers in the Union Council of Ministers, including the Prime Minister, at 15% of the total strength of the Lok Sabha.
Why A is wrong: 10% is below the constitutional ceiling.
Why B is wrong: 12% is not the figure fixed by the 91st Amendment.
Why D is wrong: 20% exceeds the limit; the cap is 15%.
Note: The same 91st Amendment also set a minimum of 12 ministers for smaller states and strengthened anti-defection rules.

Set 2 | Q.No 22 | Topic: Art & Culture | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: टिप्पाणी नृत्य के साथ आमतौर पर कौन-सा संगीत वाद्ययंत्र बजाया जाता है?
   A) ढोल और मंजीरा (छोटी झांझ)  <-- CORRECT
   B) तबला और हारमोनियम
   C) बांसुरी और वीणा
   D) सितार और सारंगी
Answer: A
Why correct: The Tippani folk dance of the Chorwad region of Gujarat is performed by women and is accompanied by percussion instruments such as the dhol and manjira (small cymbals), which set its rhythmic beat.
Why B is wrong: Tabla and harmonium are associated with Hindustani classical/semi-classical music, not the Tippani dance.
Why C is wrong: Flute and veena are melodic instruments not central to this rhythmic folk dance.
Why D is wrong: Sitar and sarangi belong to classical music traditions, not Tippani.
Note: The Tippani dance imitates the labour of women beating the floor with long sticks (tippani) to harden it.

Set 2 | Q.No 23 | Topic: Art & Culture | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: कौन-सा वेद मुख्यतः: अपनी संगीतात्मक सामग्री के लिए जाना जाता है?
   A) ऋग्वेद
   B) सामवेद  <-- CORRECT
   C) यजुर्वेद
   D) अथर्ववेद
Answer: B
Why correct: The Samaveda is the Veda of melodies and chants; its verses (saman) were meant to be sung, making it the principal source of early Indian music.
Why A is wrong: The Rigveda is the oldest Veda and contains hymns of praise, but it is not primarily musical.
Why C is wrong: The Yajurveda deals with sacrificial formulae and rituals.
Why D is wrong: The Atharvaveda contains spells, charms and everyday-life hymns.
Note: Indian classical music traces its origin to the chanting of the Samaveda.

Set 2 | Q.No 24 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: चंद्रमा पर पृथ्वी की तुलना में कम गुरुत्वाकर्षण बल क्यों लगता है?
   A) यह आकार में छोटा है
   B) इसका द्रव्यमान कम है  <-- CORRECT
   C) यह तेजी से घूमता है
   D) यह सूर्य से अधिक दूर है
Answer: B
Why correct: The Moon exerts less gravitational pull than the Earth mainly because it has much less mass (about 1/81 of Earth's mass); gravity depends on mass, so surface gravity on the Moon is about one-sixth of Earth's.
Why A is wrong: Smaller size alone does not determine gravity; it is the mass that matters, though the Moon is indeed smaller.
Why C is wrong: The Moon actually rotates slowly (tidally locked), and rotation speed does not reduce gravity.
Why D is wrong: Distance from the Sun is irrelevant to the Moon's own surface gravity.
Note: Surface gravity g = GM/R^2; the Moon's lower mass M is the dominant reason its g is about 1.62 m/s^2.

Set 2 | Q.No 25 | Topic: Books & Authors | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: द पैलेस ऑफ इल्यूजन्स के लेखक कौन हैं?
   A) चित्रा बनर्जी दिवाकरुनी  <-- CORRECT
   B) सुधा मूर्ति
   C) देवदत्त पटनायक
   D) कविता केन
Answer: A
Why correct: 'The Palace of Illusions' (2008), a retelling of the Mahabharata from Draupadi's perspective, was written by Indian-American author Chitra Banerjee Divakaruni.
Why B is wrong: Sudha Murty is known for works like 'Wise and Otherwise' and many children's books.
Why C is wrong: Devdutt Pattanaik writes on mythology (e.g. 'Jaya', 'Sita') but did not write this book.
Why D is wrong: Kavita Kane writes mythological fiction (e.g. 'Karna's Wife') but is not the author of this title.
Note: Draupadi narrates the epic in the novel, giving a strong female viewpoint of the Mahabharata.

Set 2 | Q.No 26 | Topic: Economy | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: निम्नलिखित में से कौन सा खुशी सूचकांक में उदारता कारक का उदाहरण है?
   A) राष्ट्रीय कर दरें
   B) विदेशी सहायता
   C) सरकारी सब्सिडी
   D) दान देने या दूसरों की मदद करने की इच्छा  <-- CORRECT
Answer: D
Why correct: In the World Happiness Report, 'Generosity' is measured by people's willingness to donate money or help others, reflecting prosocial behaviour in a society.
Why A is wrong: National tax rates are a fiscal-policy variable, not a measure of generosity.
Why B is wrong: Foreign aid is given between governments and is not the generosity factor of the index.
Why C is wrong: Government subsidies are state transfers, not the voluntary giving that generosity captures.
Note: The World Happiness Report ranks countries using six key factors, including GDP per capita, social support and generosity.

Set 2 | Q.No 27 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: पृथ्वी का चुंबकीय क्षेत्र हमें आवेशित सौर कणों से संरक्षित करता है। जब पृथ्वी का चुंबकीय क्षेत्र अस्थायी रूप से दुर्बल हो जाता है, तो क्या होता है?
   A) ध्रुवीय ज्योति और विकिरण जोखिम में वृद्धि होती है  <-- CORRECT
   B) वायुमंडल की पूर्ण हानि होती है
   C) गुरुत्वाकर्षण में वृद्धि होती है
   D) कोई प्रभाव नहीं होता है
Answer: A
Why correct: Earth's magnetic field deflects charged solar particles. When it weakens temporarily, more particles reach the upper atmosphere, increasing auroral activity (polar lights) and the radiation exposure for satellites and astronauts.
Why B is wrong: A temporary weakening does not strip away the entire atmosphere.
Why C is wrong: The magnetic field has nothing to do with the strength of gravity.
Why D is wrong: There is a clear effect - increased auroras and radiation - so 'no effect' is wrong.
Note: The region of space dominated by Earth's magnetic field is called the magnetosphere.

Set 2 | Q.No 28 | Topic: Sports | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: किदाम्बी श्रीकांत किस वर्ष विश्व चैंपियनशिप के फाइनल में पहुंचने वाले पहले भारतीय पुरुष शटलर बने?
   A) 2017
   B) 2018
   C) 2021  <-- CORRECT
   D) 2022
Answer: C
Why correct: Kidambi Srikanth became the first Indian male shuttler to reach the final of the BWF World Championships in 2021 at Huelva, Spain, winning the silver medal.
Why A is wrong: 2017 was a strong Super Series year for Srikanth but not when he reached the Worlds final.
Why B is wrong: 2018 was not the year of this milestone.
Why D is wrong: 2022 is after the achievement, which took place in 2021.
Note: At the same 2021 Worlds, Lakshya Sen won bronze, making it a landmark event for Indian men's badminton.

Set 2 | Q.No 29 | Topic: Economy | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: 99 से पहले किस नीति ने कुछ उद्योगों में निजी क्षेत्र की भागीदारी को सीमित कर दिया था?
   A) Industrial Licensing Policy  <-- CORRECT
   B) Agricultural Subsidy Policy
   C) Foreign Trade Policy
   D) Public Distribution System
Answer: A
Why correct: Before the 1991 reforms, the Industrial Licensing Policy (the 'Licence Raj', based on the Industries (Development and Regulation) Act, 1951) restricted private-sector entry by requiring government licences and reserving many industries for the public sector.
Why B is wrong: Agricultural subsidy policy supports farmers and does not restrict private industry.
Why C is wrong: Foreign trade policy governs exports and imports, not domestic industrial entry.
Why D is wrong: The Public Distribution System distributes subsidised food grains, unrelated to industrial licensing.
Note: The 1991 New Industrial Policy abolished licensing for most industries, opening the economy to private and foreign investment.

Set 2 | Q.No 30 | Topic: Current Affairs | Language: Hindi

Q: वर्ष 207 में चाबहार बंदरगाह के माध्यम से भारत द्वारा पहली बार अफगानिस्तान को कौन सी वस्तु भेजी गई थी?
   A) चावल
   B) गेहूँ  <-- CORRECT
   C) तेल
   D) मशीनरी
Answer: B
Why correct: In 2017, India shipped its first consignment of wheat to Afghanistan through Iran's Chabahar Port, demonstrating the port's value as a route bypassing Pakistan.
Why A is wrong: Rice was not the commodity of this landmark first shipment.
Why C is wrong: Oil was not the cargo; Chabahar gives India access to Afghanistan/Central Asia.

Set 2 | Q.No 31 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: यौवनारंभ के दौरान पुरुषों में होने वाले परिवर्तनों के लिए मुख्य रूप से कौन-सा हार्मोन उत्तरदायी है?
   A) एस्ट्रोजन
   B) थायरोक्सिन
   C) टेस्टोस्टेरोन  <-- CORRECT
   D) एड्रिनिेलिन
Answer: C
Why correct: Testosterone is the primary male sex hormone responsible for the physical changes of puberty in boys, such as deepening of the voice, facial hair and muscle growth.
Why A is wrong: Estrogen is the primary female sex hormone driving female pubertal changes.
Why B is wrong: Thyroxine, from the thyroid gland, regulates metabolism, not male puberty specifically.
Why D is wrong: Adrenaline is the 'fight-or-flight' hormone from the adrenal medulla, not a puberty hormone.
Note: Testosterone is produced mainly in the testes; the onset of puberty is triggered by the hypothalamus releasing GnRH.

Set 2 | Q.No 32 | Topic: Current Affairs | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: हाल ही में किस सांसद को इतिहास और स्कॉलरशिप में उनके योगदान के लिए राज्यसभा के लिए मनोनीत किया गया है?
   A) उज्ज्वल निकम
   B) डॉ. मीनाक्षी जैन  <-- CORRECT
   C) हरिकृष्णन
   D) सी. सदानंदन मास्टर
Answer: B
Why correct: Historian Dr. Meenakshi Jain was nominated to the Rajya Sabha in July 2025 in recognition of her contribution to history and scholarship.
Why A is wrong: Ujjwal Nikam is a well-known public prosecutor nominated for legal/public service, not for history scholarship.
Why C is wrong: Harikishan is not the person nominated for contributions to history.
Why D is wrong: C. Sadanandan Master was nominated for social/public service, not for history scholarship.
Note: The President nominates 12 members to the Rajya Sabha for distinction in literature, science, art and social service.

Set 2 | Q.No 33 | Topic: Economy | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: राष्ट्रीय नमूना सर्वेक्षण संगठन (/550) की स्थापना किस उद्देश्य के लिए की गई थी?
   A) कृषि को बढ़ावा देना
   B) उद्योग पर नज़र रखना
   C) निर्यात को बढ़ावा देना
   D) सामाजिक-ओआर्थिक स्थितियों पर सांख्यिकीय ऑआँकड़े एकत्र करना  <-- CORRECT
Answer: D
Why correct: The National Sample Survey Organisation (NSSO) was set up to collect statistical data on socio-economic conditions through large-scale sample surveys, providing inputs for policy and the national accounts.
Why A is wrong: Promoting agriculture is the work of bodies like ICAR/NABARD, not the NSSO.
Why B is wrong: Monitoring industry through production indices is the Annual Survey of Industries / industrial statistics work, distinct from NSSO's socio-economic surveys.
Why C is wrong: Promoting exports is the role of bodies like the DGFT and EXIM Bank.
Note: The NSSO is now part of the National Statistical Office (NSO) under the Ministry of Statistics and Programme Implementation.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: निम्नलिखित में से कौन-सा राज्य बांग्लादेश के साथ सीमा साझा नहीं करता है?
   A) असम
   B) ओड़िशा  <-- CORRECT
   C) त्रिपुरा
   D) पश्चिम बंगाल
Answer: B
Why correct: Odisha does not share a border with Bangladesh. Bangladesh borders the Indian states of West Bengal, Assam, Meghalaya, Tripura and Mizoram.
Why A is wrong: Assam shares a border with Bangladesh in the north-east.
Why C is wrong: Tripura is almost surrounded by Bangladesh on three sides.
Why D is wrong: West Bengal shares the longest stretch of the India-Bangladesh border.
Note: India and Bangladesh share a land border of about 4,096 km, the fifth-longest land border in the world.

Set 2 | Q.No 35 | Topic: Economy | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: निम्नलिखित में से कौन सी चुनौती आज भारतीय कृषि मे प्रमुख है?
   A) ग्रामीण क्षेत्रों में कम जनसंख्या घनत्व के कारण कृषि श्रम की कमी होना
   B) कृषि मशीनीकरण का बढ़ता स्तर
   C) कृषि जोतों का लगातार खंडित होना और परिचालन होल्डिंग्स के आकार में गिरावट  <-- CORRECT
   D) मुख्य खाद्यान्नों की घटती घरेलू मांग
Answer: C
Why correct: A major structural problem of Indian agriculture is the continuous fragmentation of landholdings due to inheritance, which steadily reduces the size of operational holdings and lowers efficiency.
Why A is wrong: Indian agriculture suffers from surplus, under-employed labour, not a shortage caused by low rural population density.
Why B is wrong: Rising mechanisation is a positive trend, not a core challenge.
Why D is wrong: Domestic demand for staple food grains is not falling; the problem is on the supply/structure side.
Note: Average operational holding size in India has fallen to roughly 1.08 hectares, making most farmers small or marginal.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: भारत के पहले निर्यात प्रसंस्करण क्षेत्र का स्थान किस भारतीय बंदरगाह को बनाया गया था?
   A) सूरत
   B) कांडला  <-- CORRECT
   C) मुंबई
   D) कोचीन
Answer: B
Why correct: India's first Export Processing Zone (EPZ) was set up at Kandla, Gujarat, in 1965 - it was also Asia's first EPZ.
Why A is wrong: Surat is a major textile/diamond hub but was not the site of the first EPZ.
Why C is wrong: Mumbai's SEEPZ came later (1973), after Kandla.
Why D is wrong: Cochin had an EPZ established later, not the first.
Note: Export Processing Zones were the forerunners of today's Special Economic Zones (SEZs).

Set 2 | Q.No 37 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: आयुर्वेद के जनक के रूप में किसे जाना जाता है?
   A) Charak  <-- CORRECT
   B) Vagbhata
   C) Sushruta
   D) Nagarjuna
Answer: A
Why correct: Charak (Charaka) is regarded as the father of Ayurveda (Indian medicine); his treatise, the Charaka Samhita, is the foundational text of Ayurvedic internal medicine.
Why B is wrong: Vagbhata was a later Ayurvedic scholar who compiled the Ashtanga Hridayam.
Why C is wrong: Sushruta is honoured as the father of surgery (Sushruta Samhita), not of Ayurveda as a whole.
Why D is wrong: Nagarjuna was a scholar associated with alchemy/rasashastra, not the founding of Ayurveda.
Note: Charaka served in the court of the Kushan emperor Kanishka and emphasised prevention and a balanced lifestyle.

Set 2 | Q.No 38 | Topic: History | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: बिम्बिसार की कथित तौर पर हत्या करने या उसे आत्महत्या के लिए मजबूर करने के बाद उसका उत्तराधिकारी कौन बना था?
   A) अशोक
   B) बिंदुसार
   C) अजातशत्रु  <-- CORRECT
   D) चंद्रगुप्त मौर्य
Answer: C
Why correct: According to tradition, Ajatashatru succeeded his father Bimbisara as ruler of Magadha after imprisoning and reportedly causing his death.
Why A is wrong: Ashoka was a much later Mauryan emperor, not Bimbisara's successor.
Why B is wrong: Bindusara was a Mauryan king (Ashoka's father), unrelated to Bimbisara's succession.
Why D is wrong: Chandragupta Maurya founded the Mauryan empire long after Bimbisara's Haryanka dynasty.
Note: Bimbisara and Ajatashatru belonged to the Haryanka dynasty of Magadha and were contemporaries of the Buddha and Mahavira.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: निम्नलिखित में से किस वर्ष में औरंगजेब की मृत्यु हुई थी?
   A) 1707  <-- CORRECT
   B) 1717
   C) 1747
   D) 1757
Answer: A
Why correct: The Mughal emperor Aurangzeb died in 1707 (at Ahmednagar), an event that is often taken to mark the beginning of the decline of the Mughal Empire.
Why B is wrong: 1717 is incorrect; by then Farrukhsiyar was on the throne.
Why C is wrong: 1747 is unrelated to Aurangzeb's death.
Why D is wrong: 1757 is the year of the Battle of Plassey, not Aurangzeb's death.
Note: Aurangzeb ruled for about 49 years (1658-1707), the longest reign of any Mughal emperor.

Set 2 | Q.No 40 | Topic: Polity & Constitution | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: जुलाई 2025 तक, भारत में कितने राज्य हैं जिन्होंने पंचायती राज संस्थाओं में महिलाओं के लिए 50% आरक्षण का प्रावधान किया है?
   A) 21  <-- CORRECT
   B) 11
   C) 14
   D) 25
Answer: A
Why correct: As of July 2025, about 21 states/UTs had provided for 50% reservation for women in Panchayati Raj Institutions, going beyond the constitutional minimum of one-third.
Why B is wrong: 11 understates the number of states that have adopted 50% reservation.
Why C is wrong: 14 is lower than the figure reported.
Why D is wrong: 25 overstates the number of states with the 50% provision.
Note: The 73rd Constitutional Amendment (1992) mandates at least one-third reservation for women in panchayats; many states have raised it to 50%.

Set 3 | Q.No 21 | Topic: Polity & Constitution | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: किसी राज्य में राष्ट्रपति शासन की सिफारिश करने का अधिकार किसके पास होता है?
   A) मुख्यमंत्री
   B) राज्यपाल  <-- CORRECT
   C) प्रधानमंत्री
   D) सर्वोच्च न्यायालय
Answer: B
Why correct: The Governor of a state sends a report to the President recommending President's Rule (Article 356) when the state government cannot function according to the Constitution.
Why A is wrong: The Chief Minister heads the state government that is being superseded; he does not recommend President's Rule.
Why C is wrong: The Prime Minister advises on national matters but does not formally recommend state emergency.
Why D is wrong: The Supreme Court can review the proclamation but does not recommend its imposition.
Note: President's Rule under Article 356 must be approved by Parliament within two months and the S.R. Bommai (1994) judgment made it subject to judicial review.

Set 3 | Q.No 22 | Topic: Polity & Constitution | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: जब राज्य विधानसभा में किसी भी पार्टी को स्पष्ट बहुमत न हो तो मुख्यमंत्री की नियुक्ति का अधिकार किसके पास होता है?
   A) राष्ट्रपति
   B) विधानसभा का अध्यक्ष
   C) प्रधानमंत्री
   D) राज्यपाल  <-- CORRECT
Answer: D
Why correct: When no party has a clear majority in the state assembly, the Governor uses discretion to appoint as Chief Minister the person most likely to command the confidence of the House.
Why A is wrong: The President is concerned with the Union government, not appointing a state CM.
Why B is wrong: The Speaker of the Assembly presides over the House but does not appoint the CM.
Why C is wrong: The Prime Minister has no role in appointing a state Chief Minister.
Note: The Governor's discretion here is one of the few genuine discretionary powers under the Constitution, exercised especially in hung assemblies.

Set 3 | Q.No 23 | Topic: Art & Culture | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: ऐतिहासिक अवलोकन के अनुसार भारतीय संगीत के इतिहास का अध्ययन करने के लिए सबसे पहले किन तत्वों को समझना आवश्यक है?
   A) मानव सभ्यता और भाषा
   B) मानव विकास और तकनीकी कौशल
   C) मानव उत्पत्ति और ध्वनि, स्वर और लय जैसे तत्व  <-- CORRECT
   D) वाद्ययंत्रों और नृत्य का विकास
Answer: C
Why correct: To study the history of Indian music, one must first understand human origin and the basic elements of sound - swara (tone), and laya (rhythm) - from which all music developed.
Why A is wrong: Human civilisation and language are background context, but music specifically rests on sound, tone and rhythm.
Why B is wrong: Human evolution and technical skill are too general and not the core musical elements.
Why D is wrong: The development of instruments and dance came after the fundamental elements of sound.
Note: Indian classical theory is built on the concepts of swara (notes), raga (melodic framework) and tala (rhythmic cycle).

Set 3 | Q.No 24 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: यदि दो वस्तुओं के बीच की दूरी छह गुना बढ़ जाए तो गुरुत्वाकर्षण बल पर क्या प्रभाव पड़ेगा?
   A) 36 गुना बड़ा हो जाता है
   B) 6 गुना बड़ा हो जाता है
   C) 36 गुना छोटा हो जाता है  <-- CORRECT
   D) /6 गुना छोटा हो जाता है
Answer: C
Why correct: By Newton's law of gravitation, force is inversely proportional to the square of the distance. If the distance increases 6 times, the force becomes 1/6^2 = 1/36, i.e. 36 times smaller.
Why A is wrong: Force decreases, not increases, when distance grows, so '36 times larger' is wrong.
Why B is wrong: Force does not increase 6 times; it decreases with the square of distance.
Why D is wrong: Force falls by the square (1/36), not just 1/6.
Note: Newton's law: F = G m1 m2 / r^2, the inverse-square law of gravitation.

   B) मास्टर ऑफ द गेम
   C) मॉर्निंग, नून एंड नाइट
   D) ब्लडलाइन
Answer: A
Why correct: 'Memories of Midnight' (1990) is Sidney Sheldon's sequel to his earlier bestseller 'The Other Side of Midnight'.
Why B is wrong: 'Master of the Game' is a separate Sidney Sheldon novel, not a sequel to The Other Side of Midnight.
Why C is wrong: 'Morning, Noon and Night' is another standalone Sheldon novel.
Why D is wrong: 'Bloodline' is a different Sidney Sheldon thriller, not the sequel.
Note: Both novels follow the character Catherine Alexander and the schemes of Constantin Demiris.

Set 3 | Q.No 26 | Topic: Geography | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: मालवा पठार मुख्यतः: किस राज्य में स्थित है?
   A) मध्य प्रदेश  <-- CORRECT
   B) महाराष्ट्र
   C) राजस्थान
   D) गुजरात
Answer: A
Why correct: The Malwa Plateau lies mainly in Madhya Pradesh (extending into parts of Rajasthan and Gujarat) and is a volcanic, black-soil plateau in west-central India.
Why B is wrong: Maharashtra is associated with the Deccan Plateau, not the Malwa Plateau.
Why C is wrong: Only the north-western fringe of Malwa touches Rajasthan; the plateau is principally in MP.
Why D is wrong: Gujarat lies to the west and holds only a small edge of the region.
Note: The Malwa Plateau is drained by rivers like the Chambal and Betwa and is known for its fertile black soil.

Set 3 | Q.No 27 | Topic: Geography | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: भाबर क्षेत्र भारत की किस भौतिक विशेषता से जुड़ा हुआ है?
   A) हिमालय की तलहटी  <-- CORRECT
   B) प्रायद्वीपीय पठार
   C) सिंधु-गंगा का मैदान
   D) रेगिस्तानी क्षेत्र
Answer: A
Why correct: The Bhabar is a narrow belt of porous, pebbly soil at the foothills of the Himalayas, where rivers descending from the mountains deposit coarse sediments and streams often disappear underground.
Why B is wrong: The Peninsular Plateau is an ancient landmass of the south, unrelated to the Bhabar.
Why C is wrong: The Indo-Gangetic plain lies south of the Bhabar; the Terai (not Bhabar) adjoins it.
Why D is wrong: The Bhabar is a humid foothill zone, not a desert region.
Note: Just south of the Bhabar lies the marshy Terai belt, where the underground streams re-emerge.

   B) विश्व बैंक

   A) 1932
   B) 1972  <-- CORRECT
   C) 1980
   D) 1992

Set 3 | Q.No 30 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: एक इंजीनियर को रडार का इस्तेमाल करके धरती की सतह में होने वाले बदलावों पर नज़र रखने का काम सौंपा गया है, यहाँ तक कि बादलों के बीच और रात में भी।
   A) Chandrayaan-3
   B) EOS-09
   C) NISAR  <-- CORRECT
   D) XPoSat
Answer: C
Why correct: NISAR (NASA-ISRO Synthetic Aperture Radar) is a joint Earth-observation satellite that uses radar to monitor changes in the Earth's surface in all weather, day or night, even through clouds.
Why A is wrong: Chandrayaan-3 is India's lunar lander-rover mission, not an Earth-surface radar satellite.
Why B is wrong: EOS-09 is an Earth-observation satellite but is not the NASA-ISRO radar collaboration described.
Why D is wrong: XPoSat is an X-ray polarimetry satellite for studying cosmic sources, not Earth's surface.
Note: NISAR carries dual-frequency (L- and S-band) radar, the first satellite of its kind, to track land deformation, ice and ecosystems.

   C) SSLV
   D) ASLV

Why correct: The GSLV Mk III (now called LVM3) is nicknamed the 'Fat Boy' because of its heavy, bulky build; it is ISRO's most powerful launch vehicle.
Why A is wrong: The PSLV (Polar Satellite Launch Vehicle) is ISRO's reliable workhorse, not the 'Fat Boy'.
Why C is wrong: The SSLV is the Small Satellite Launch Vehicle, a lightweight rocket.
Why D is wrong: The ASLV was an early, much smaller experimental launch vehicle.

   A) लेफ्टिनेंट कमांडर यशस्वी सोलंकी  <-- CORRECT

   D) कैप्टन शिखा शर्मा

Set 3 | Q.No 33 | Topic: Economy | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: किस नीति ने लघु उद्योगों को प्रमुखता से बढ़ावा दिया?
   A) Industrial Policy of 1948
   B) Industrial Policy of 1956
   C) Industrial Policy of 1977  <-- CORRECT
   D) Industrial Policy of 1980
Answer: C
Why correct: The Industrial Policy of 1977 (under the Janata government) gave special prominence to small-scale and cottage industries, expanding the list of items reserved for them and promoting decentralised development.
Why A is wrong: The 1948 policy laid the first framework for a mixed economy but did not specially emphasise small industries.
Why B is wrong: The 1956 policy emphasised heavy industry and the public sector ('commanding heights').
Why D is wrong: The 1980 policy focused on raising productivity and reviving the public sector, not chiefly on small industry.
Note: The 1977 policy introduced the concept of 'District Industries Centres' to promote small enterprises.

Set 3 | Q.No 34 | Topic: Geography | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: भारत में पहली तेल रिफाइनरी कहाँ स्थापित की गई थी?
   A) हल्दिया
   B) कोयली
   C) बरौनी
   D) डिगबोई  <-- CORRECT
Answer: D
Why correct: India's first oil refinery was established at Digboi in Assam (commissioned in 1901), making it one of the oldest operating refineries in the world.
Why A is wrong: Haldia in West Bengal has a much later refinery.
Why B is wrong: Koyali (Gujarat) refinery came up in the 1960s.
Why C is wrong: Barauni refinery in Bihar was set up in the 1960s.
Note: Digboi is often called the 'Oil City of Asia'; oil was first struck there in the 1880s.

Set 3 | Q.No 35 | Topic: Economy | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: जब नाममात्र सकल घरेलू उत्पाद (८07?) वास्तविक जीडीपी (८0?) की तुलना में तेज़ी से बढ़ता है, तो यह __ दर्शाता है
   A) शून्य वृद्धि
   B) गिरती मुद्रास्फीति
   C) उच्च मुद्रास्फीति  <-- CORRECT
   D) अपस्फीति
Answer: C
Why correct: If nominal GDP rises faster than real GDP, the gap is due to rising prices - this indicates high inflation, because nominal GDP is measured at current prices while real GDP is adjusted for price changes.
Why A is wrong: Zero growth would mean GDP is not changing, which is not the case here.
Why B is wrong: Falling inflation would narrow, not widen, the gap between nominal and real GDP.
Why D is wrong: Deflation means falling prices, which would make nominal GDP grow slower than real GDP.
Note: The ratio of nominal to real GDP is the GDP deflator, a broad measure of economy-wide inflation.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------

   B) कुछ व्यापारिक साझेदारों पर अत्यधिक निर्भरता

   D) उच्च शुल्क संरचना
Answer: C
Why correct: The main weakness of India's balance of trade is a persistent trade deficit - the value of imports (especially crude oil, gold and electronics) consistently exceeds the value of exports.
Why A is wrong: A surplus in services exports is actually a strength that partly offsets the goods deficit, not a weakness.
Why B is wrong: Over-dependence on a few partners is a concern but not the defining weakness of the trade balance.
Why D is wrong: A high tariff structure is a policy feature, not the core trade-balance problem.
Note: India's large software and services exports help finance its merchandise (goods) trade deficit in the current account.

   B) सकल घरेलू उत्पाद, सकल राष्ट्रीय आय, साक्षरता

Set 4 | Q.No 29 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: 4,000 वर्ष (मिलेनकोविच चक्र) में पृथ्वी के अक्ष का झुकाव 22.* से 24.5" के बीच बदलता रहता है। यह परिवर्तन पृथ्वी को किस प्रकार प्रभावित करता है?
   A) अधिक झुकाव से मौसमी विपर्यास में वृद्धि होती है  <-- CORRECT
   B) झुकाव परिवर्तन से कक्षीय चाल बदलता है
   C) झुकाव परिवर्तन चुंबकीय क्षेत्र को प्रभावित करता है
   D) कोई प्रभाव नहीं होता है
Answer: A
Why correct: Over the roughly 41,000-year Milankovitch cycle, Earth's axial tilt (obliquity) varies between about 22.1 and 24.5 degrees; a greater tilt increases the contrast between seasons (hotter summers, colder winters).
Why B is wrong: A change in axial tilt does not change the Earth's orbital speed.
Why C is wrong: Obliquity affects climate/seasons, not the planet's magnetic field.
Why D is wrong: There is a clear climatic effect, so 'no effect' is wrong.
Note: Milankovitch cycles - changes in eccentricity, obliquity and precession - drive long-term ice-age cycles.

   C) ऐच्छिक क्रिया
   D) समन्वित क्रिया
Answer: B
Why correct: The heartbeat is an involuntary action - it occurs automatically and continuously without conscious control, driven by the heart's own pacemaker.

Set 4 | Q.No 39 | Topic: History | Language: Hindi

Q: 946 के प्रांतीय चुनावों के दौरान किस राजनीतिक दल ने "सामान्य" निर्वाचन क्षेत्रों में अच्छा प्रदर्शन किया था?
   A) भारतीय राष्ट्रीय कांग्रेस  <-- CORRECT
   B) जस्टिस पार्टी
   C) भारतीय कम्युनिस्ट पार्टी
   D) स्वराज पार्टी
Answer: A
Why correct: In the 1946 provincial elections, the Indian National Congress performed very well in the 'general' (non-Muslim) constituencies, winning a large majority of those seats.
Why B is wrong: The Justice Party had declined by 1946 and was not a major winner.
Why C is wrong: The Communist Party of India won only a handful of seats.
Why D is wrong: The Swaraj Party was a 1920s formation and no longer a separate force in 1946.
Note: The Muslim League won most of the Muslim-reserved seats in 1946, strengthening its demand for Pakistan.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: भारत रत्न पुरस्कार प्राप्त करने वाली पहली महिला कौन थी?
   A) अरुणा आसफ अली
   B) लता दीनानाथ मंगेशकर

   D) मदर मैरी टेरेसा

Why correct: Indira Gandhi was the first woman to receive the Bharat Ratna, India's highest civilian award, in 1971.
Why A is wrong: Aruna Asaf Ali received the Bharat Ratna in 1997, much later.
Why B is wrong: Lata Mangeshkar received the Bharat Ratna in 2001.
Why D is wrong: Mother Teresa received the Nobel Peace Prize (1979) but not the Bharat Ratna.

Set 5 | Q.No 21 | Topic: Polity & Constitution | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Which body recommends the distribution of tax revenues between union and states?
   A) NITI Aayog
   B) Parliament
   C) Finance Commission  <-- CORRECT
   D) Planning Commission
Answer: C
Why correct: The Finance Commission (Article 280) recommends the distribution of the net proceeds of taxes between the Union and the States and the principles governing grants-in-aid to the States.
Why A is wrong: NITI Aayog is an advisory think-tank with no role in tax devolution.
Why B is wrong: Parliament legislates on taxes but does not recommend the sharing formula.
Why D is wrong: The Planning Commission, now abolished, dealt with development planning, not tax devolution.
Note: The Finance Commission is constituted by the President every five years (or earlier if needed).

Set 5 | Q.No 22 | Topic: Polity & Constitution | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: During a financial emergency under Article 360, the president can:
   A) Reduce salaries of government employees  <-- CORRECT
   B) Dismiss State Governments
   C) Dissolve Parliament
   D) Suspend Fundamental Rights
Answer: A
Why correct: During a Financial Emergency under Article 360, the President can direct the reduction of salaries and allowances of government employees, including judges of the Supreme Court and High Courts, to maintain financial stability.
Why B is wrong: Dismissing state governments is a feature of President's Rule under Article 356, not a Financial Emergency.
Why C is wrong: Dissolving Parliament is not a power granted under Article 360.
Why D is wrong: Suspension of Fundamental Rights is linked to a National Emergency under Article 352, not a Financial Emergency.
Note: A Financial Emergency under Article 360 has never been declared in India.

Set 5 | Q.No 23 | Topic: Art & Culture | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Why is the Raga Tarangini considered highly important in Hindustani music history?
   A) It uses only southern raga's
   B) It introduces tabla and harmonium
   C) It uses many raga names still in use today  <-- CORRECT
   D) It rejects traditional Indian theories
Answer: C
Why correct: The Raga Tarangini is considered historically important because it records and uses many raga names that are still in use in Hindustani music today, providing continuity with earlier tradition.
Why A is wrong: It does not deal only with southern (Carnatic) ragas; it is a Hindustani-music text.
Why B is wrong: It is a treatise on ragas, not a work introducing the tabla and harmonium.
Why D is wrong: It builds on, rather than rejects, traditional Indian musical theory.
Note: Raga Tarangini was authored by Locana (Lochana Kavi), an early text valuable for the history of ragas.

Set 5 | Q.No 24 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Archimedes’ principle states that a body immersed in a fluid experiences an upward force equal to
   A) Its own weight
   B) The volume of the body
   C) The weight of the fluid displaced  <-- CORRECT
   D) The density of the fluid
Answer: C
Why correct: Archimedes' principle states that a body immersed (fully or partly) in a fluid experiences an upward buoyant force equal to the weight of the fluid it displaces.
Why A is wrong: The buoyant force equals the displaced fluid's weight, not the body's own weight (these are equal only when the body floats).
Why B is wrong: The volume of the body is a quantity, not a force.
Why D is wrong: Density of the fluid alone is not a force; the upthrust depends on weight of fluid displaced.
Note: This principle explains why ships float and why objects feel lighter in water.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Which poetic collection by Sumitranandan Pant won him the Jnanpith Award?
   A) Pallav
   B) Kala Aur Budhdha Chand
   C) Chidambara  <-- CORRECT
   D) Veena
Answer: C
Why correct: The poetic collection 'Chidambara' won Sumitranandan Pant the Jnanpith Award (for 1968), making him one of the early recipients of the honour.
Why A is wrong: 'Pallav' is an earlier important collection by Pant but did not win him the Jnanpith.
Why B is wrong: 'Kala Aur Budhdha Chand' is another of his works, not the Jnanpith-winning one.
Why D is wrong: 'Veena' was one of his early collections, not the award-winning book.
Note: Sumitranandan Pant was a leading poet of the Chhayavaad (Romantic) movement in Hindi literature.

Set 5 | Q.No 26 | Topic: Geography | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: The Sunderbans Delta is formed by the confluence of which rivers?
   A) Ganga and Yamuna
   B) Ganga and Brahmaputra  <-- CORRECT
   C) Godavari and Krishna
   D) Mahanadi and Godavari
Answer: B
Why correct: The Sundarbans delta is formed by the confluence of the Ganga, Brahmaputra and Meghana rivers; among the options, the Ganga and Brahmaputra are the principal rivers.
Why A is wrong: The Yamuna is a tributary of the Ganga and does not directly form the Sundarbans delta.
Why C is wrong: The Godavari and Krishna form deltas on the eastern (Andhra) coast.
Why D is wrong: The Mahanadi and Godavari form separate deltas, not the Sundarbans.
Note: The Sundarbans is the world's largest mangrove forest and home to the Royal Bengal Tiger.

Set 5 | Q.No 27 | Topic: Geography | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: The Himalayas are wider in which sector of India?
   A) Western Himalayas  <-- CORRECT
   B) Central Himalayas
   C) Eastern Himalayas
   D) Shiwalik Himalayas
Answer: A
Why correct: The Himalayas are widest in the Western (Kashmir) sector and progressively narrow towards the east; the western Himalayas span the greatest north-south width.
Why B is wrong: The Central Himalayas (Nepal region) are narrower than the western sector.
Why C is wrong: The Eastern Himalayas are the narrowest but rise very steeply.
Why D is wrong: The Shiwaliks are only the outermost, lowest range, not a 'wider' sector of the whole system.
Note: The Himalayas are divided into the Western, Central and Eastern sectors, and the highest peak, Mount Everest, lies in the Central (Nepal) Himalayas.

   B) 5
   C) 6  <-- CORRECT
   D) 7
Answer: C

Why A is wrong: Four is fewer than the six factors used.
Why B is wrong: Five omits one of the standard factors.
Why D is wrong: Seven is one more than the six key variables.
Note: Finland has topped the World Happiness Report for several consecutive years.

Set 5 | Q.No 31 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Which telescope provided the first direct image of a black hole?
   A) Hubble
   B) Event Horizon Telescope  <-- CORRECT
   C) Spitzer
   D) Kepler
Answer: B
Why correct: The Event Horizon Telescope (EHT) produced the first-ever direct image of a black hole - the supermassive black hole at the centre of galaxy M87 - released in April 2019.
Why A is wrong: The Hubble Space Telescope is an optical/UV observatory and did not capture the first black-hole image.
Why C is wrong: The Spitzer Space Telescope was an infrared observatory, not the source of this image.
Why D is wrong: The Kepler telescope was designed to detect exoplanets, not image black holes.
Note: The EHT is a global network of radio telescopes that works together as an Earth-sized virtual telescope.

Set 5 | Q.No 32 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: if an astronaut’s mass is 70 kg, what will be their weight on the Moon (1/6th of Earth's gravity)?
   A) 700 N
   B) 117 N  <-- CORRECT
   C) 420 N
   D) 686 N
Answer: B
Why correct: Weight on the Moon = mass x lunar gravity = 70 kg x (9.8/6) m/s^2 ≈ 70 x 1.63 ≈ 114-117 N.
Why A is wrong: 700 N (using g = 10) would be the approximate weight on Earth, not the Moon.
Why C is wrong: 420 N would imply gravity far higher than one-sixth of Earth's.
Why D is wrong: 686 N (70 x 9.8) is the weight on Earth, not on the Moon.
Note: Mass stays constant everywhere; only weight (= mass x local gravity) changes between the Earth and the Moon.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------

   A) 1950s
   B) 1960s  <-- CORRECT
   C) 1970s
   D) 1980s
Answer: B
Why correct: The Minimum Support Price (MSP) system was introduced in the 1960s (around 1966-67) during the Green Revolution to assure farmers a guaranteed price and encourage food-grain production.
Why A is wrong: The 1950s pre-dates the MSP mechanism.
Why C is wrong: The 1970s is after MSP had already been introduced.
Why D is wrong: The 1980s is much later than the actual introduction.
Note: MSP is announced by the government on the recommendation of the Commission for Agricultural Costs and Prices (CACP).

   D) Pralay

Set 5 | Q.No 36 | Topic: Economy | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Which index measures wholesale prices?
   A) Gross Domestic Product Deflator
   B) Consumer Price Index
   C) Index of Industrial Production
   D) Wholesale Price Index  <-- CORRECT
Answer: D
Why correct: The Wholesale Price Index (WPI) measures the average change in prices of goods at the wholesale level (bulk transactions between businesses).
Why A is wrong: The GDP deflator measures economy-wide price change, not specifically wholesale prices.
Why B is wrong: The Consumer Price Index (CPI) measures prices at the retail (consumer) level.
Why C is wrong: The Index of Industrial Production (IIP) measures output/production volume, not prices.
Note: In India, WPI is released by the Office of the Economic Adviser, while CPI is released by the National Statistical Office.

Set 5 | Q.No 37 | Topic: Economy | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Which structural constraint continues to be the most critical factor limiting agricultural productivity in India?
   A) inadequacy of fertile soils across major regions
   B) High dependence on monsoonal variability  <-- CORRECT
   C) Chronic shortage of agricultural labor
   D) Weakness of domestic market linkages
Answer: B
Why correct: High dependence on the monsoon (rainfall variability) is the most critical structural constraint on Indian agricultural productivity, since a large share of farmland is rain-fed and vulnerable to erratic rains.
Why A is wrong: India has substantial fertile soil; inadequacy of fertile soil is not the principal constraint.
Why C is wrong: India generally has surplus agricultural labour, not a chronic shortage.
Why D is wrong: Weak market linkages are a problem but not the most critical productivity constraint.
Note: About half of India's net sown area is still rain-fed, which is why irrigation expansion is a policy priority.

Answer: B

Why A is wrong: November 2024 is not when the official announcement was made.
Why C is wrong: January 2025 is after the December 2024 announcement.
Why D is wrong: October 2024 is incorrect.

   C) Maharashtra
   D) Punjab

Why B is wrong: Odisha was not the region of Henry Lawrence's command.

Set 6 | Q.No 21 | Topic: Polity & Constitution | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: संविधान की कौन सी अनुसूची संघ और राज्यों के बीच शक्तियों के विभाजन को निर्दिष्ट करती है?
   A) 5th Schedule
   B) 7th Schedule  <-- CORRECT
   C) 9th Schedule
   D) 10th Schedule
Answer: B
Why correct: The Seventh Schedule of the Constitution divides legislative powers between the Union and the States through three lists - the Union List, the State List and the Concurrent List.
Why A is wrong: The Fifth Schedule deals with the administration of Scheduled Areas and Scheduled Tribes.
Why C is wrong: The Ninth Schedule contains laws protected from judicial review (mainly land-reform laws).
Why D is wrong: The Tenth Schedule contains the anti-defection provisions.
Note: The Union List has the most subjects, and on the Concurrent List a Union law prevails over a conflicting State law.

Q: राज्यपाल को उनके पद की शपथ किसके द्वारा दिलाई जाती है?
   A) राष्ट्रपति
   B) प्रधानमंत्री
   C) उच्च न्यायालय के मुख्य न्यायाधीश  <-- CORRECT
   D) मुख्यमंत्री

Why D is wrong: The Chief Minister is himself sworn in by the Governor, not the other way round.

Q: टिप्पणी नृत्य की प्राथमिक विशेषता क्या है?
   A) लयबद्ध नृत्य करते समय नर्तकों द्वारा “टिप्पणी” नामक छड़ियों का प्रयोग  <-- CORRECT
   B) तलवारों और ढालों से तलवारबाजी
   C) धीमी और सुंदर गति के साथ एकल नृत्य
   D) रूमाल का गोलाकार गति में उपयोग

Set 6 | Q.No 26 | Topic: Geography | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------

   A) केरल तट
   B) मावसिनराम, मेघालय  <-- CORRECT
   C) कोंकण तट
   D) पश्चिमी राजस्थान

Set 6 | Q.No 29 | Topic: Art & Culture | Language: Hindi

   B) कोलकाता

   D) चेन्नई
Answer: C

Set 6 | Q.No 30 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: यूरेनस का अक्षीय झुकाव (8:09 (॥) लगभग 98" है, यानी यह लगभग अपने पार्श्र (30६6) पर घूर्णन करता है। इसका यूरेनस के मौसमों पर क्या प्रभाव पड़ता है?
   A) अत्यधिक मौसमी परिवर्तन  <-- CORRECT
   B) कोई मौसमी परिवर्तन नहीं होता है
   C) मृदु मौसम
   D) एक पार्श्श पर स्थायी दिन
Answer: A
Why correct: Uranus has an axial tilt of about 98 degrees, so it rotates almost on its side; this produces extreme seasonal variation, with each pole facing the Sun continuously for about 42 years.
Why B is wrong: With such an extreme tilt there are very strong seasonal changes, not none.
Why C is wrong: The seasons are extreme, not mild.
Why D is wrong: While a pole does get long days, the overall effect is extreme seasonal change, which option A captures best.
Note: Uranus's extreme tilt is thought to have resulted from a massive collision early in the solar system's history.

Set 6 | Q.No 31 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: 00 प्रकाश वर्ष दूर स्थित किसी तारे से प्रकाश को पृथ्वी तक पहुँचने में लगभग 00 वर्ष लगते हैं। विस्फोट के बाद (यदि वह अभी विस्फोट करता है) तारा हमें कितने समय तक दिखाई देगा?
   A) Immediately
   B) After 100 years  <-- CORRECT
   C) After 1 year
   D) Never
Answer: B
Why correct: Light from a star 100 light-years away takes 100 years to reach Earth, so if the star explodes now, we would see the explosion only after 100 years.
Why A is wrong: Light is not instantaneous; it travels at a finite speed.
Why C is wrong: One year is far too short for light to cross 100 light-years.
Why D is wrong: We will eventually see it - after the 100-year light-travel time.
Note: Because of this delay, when we look at distant stars we are effectively seeing them as they were in the past.

Set 7 | Q.No 24 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: प्रतिध्वनि को स्पष्ट रूप से सुनने के लिए ध्वनि के स्रोत से बाधा की न्यूनतम दूरी होती है
   A) 34.4 m
   B) 22.5 m
   C) 17.2 m  <-- CORRECT
   D) 10.6 m
Answer: C
Why correct: To hear a distinct echo, the reflected sound must return after at least 0.1 s; with sound speed about 344 m/s, the obstacle must be at least (344 x 0.1)/2 = 17.2 m away.
Why A is wrong: 34.4 m is the total path (to and back), not the one-way minimum distance.
Why B is wrong: 22.5 m does not correspond to the 0.1-second persistence-of-hearing limit.
Why D is wrong: 10.6 m is too short; the echo would merge with the original sound.
Note: The 0.1-second limit comes from the persistence of sound in human ears.

Why C is wrong: There were three schedules, not four.
Why D is wrong: Five is not the number of categories under the 1956 resolution.
Note: Schedule A reserved key industries for the State; the 1956 resolution gave the public sector the 'commanding heights' of the economy.

Set 7 | Q.No 36 | Topic: Economy | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: यदि सरकार संकुचनकारी राजकोषीय नीति अपनाती है, तो____
   A) सार्वजनिक व्यय को कम करता है या करों को बढ़ाता है।  <-- CORRECT
   B) अधिक पैसा छापता है।
   C) करों को कम करता है।
   D) सार्वजनिक व्यय बढ़ाता है।
Answer: A
Why correct: Under a contractionary fiscal policy the government reduces public expenditure and/or raises taxes to cut aggregate demand, typically to control inflation.
Why B is wrong: Printing more money is monetary expansion by the central bank, not fiscal policy.
Why C is wrong: Cutting taxes is an expansionary fiscal measure.
Why D is wrong: Increasing public expenditure is also expansionary, the opposite of contractionary.
Note: Fiscal policy concerns government spending and taxation, while monetary policy concerns money supply and interest rates.

   B) 3  <-- CORRECT

   B) প্রধানমন্ত্রী এটি ভেঙে দিতে পারেন।

   A) তাৎপর্যপূর্ণভাবে উষ্ণতর
   B) একই তাপমাত্রা  <-- CORRECT
   C) শীতল

Note: As a percentage of geographical area, the north-eastern states (like Mizoram) lead, but in absolute area Madhya Pradesh is first.

Set 8 | Q.No 38 | Topic: History | Language: Bengali
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: ব্রিটিশদের দ্বারা প্রবর্তিত চিরস্থায়ী বন্দোবস্তের অধীনে, জমিদারদের উপর প্রধান দায়িত্ব কী ছিল?
   A) নিজেরাই জমি চাষ করবে
   B) কৃষকদের কাছ থেকে খাজনা আদায় করা এবং কোম্পানিকে রাজস্ব প্রদান করা  <-- CORRECT
   C) ব্রিটিশদের সাথে পণ্য বাণিজ্য
   D) বাণিজ্য রুট পরিচালনা করা
Answer: B
Why correct: Under the Permanent Settlement (introduced by Lord Cornwallis in 1793), the zamindars' chief duty was to collect rent from the peasants and pay a fixed revenue to the Company.
Why A is wrong: Zamindars were intermediaries who collected rent, not cultivators of the land themselves.
Why C is wrong: Trading goods with the British was not the zamindar's defined duty.
Why D is wrong: Managing trade routes was not part of the Permanent Settlement obligations.
Note: The Permanent Settlement fixed the land revenue permanently, but harsh terms often ruined both zamindars and peasants.

Q: ট্রান্সপারেন্সি ইন্টারন্যাশনাল কোন প্রতিবেদন প্রকাশ করে না? I. গণতন্ত্র সূচক Il. দুনীতির ধারণা সূচক
   A) Only I  <-- CORRECT

   D) Neither I nor II

Q: The Council of Ministers in a state is collectively responsible to:
   A) President
   B) Supreme Court
   C) Governor
   D) State Legislature  <-- CORRECT
Answer: D
Why correct: In a state, the Council of Ministers is collectively responsible to the State Legislative Assembly (the directly elected House), mirroring the Union arrangement with the Lok Sabha.
Why A is wrong: The President is the head of the Union, not the body to which a state ministry answers.
Why B is wrong: The Supreme Court is a judicial body, not one to which ministers are politically responsible.
Why C is wrong: The Governor is the constitutional head of the state but the ministry is responsible to the Assembly.
Note: Collective responsibility means if the Assembly passes a no-confidence motion, the entire Council of Ministers must resign.

   D) Article 110

Why A is wrong: Article 107 deals with the introduction and passing of bills generally.
Why C is wrong: Article 109 deals with the special procedure for Money Bills.
Why D is wrong: Article 110 defines what a Money Bill is.
Note: A joint sitting is presided over by the Speaker of the Lok Sabha; it cannot be used for Money Bills or Constitutional Amendment Bills.

Why C is wrong: The Guru-Shishya tradition is central to classical music; folk/tribal music spreads more broadly through oral community practice.

------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: The rolling of thunder is mainly due to
   A) Resonance of clouds
   B) Successive reflections of sound  <-- CORRECT
   C) Lightning effect
   D) Interference of sound waves
Answer: B
Why correct: The rolling of thunder is mainly due to the successive reflections of the sound of the lightning discharge from clouds, hills and the ground, which reach the listener at slightly different times.
Why A is wrong: Resonance of clouds is not the cause of the prolonged rumble.
Why C is wrong: The lightning is the source of the sound, but the 'rolling' is from reflections.
Why D is wrong: Interference of waves is not the principal reason for the rumbling sound.
Note: We see lightning before we hear thunder because light travels much faster than sound.

   B) Adam Smith
   C) Hicks
   D) Ricardo  <-- CORRECT
Answer: D

Why A is wrong: Keynes is known for macroeconomics and demand management.
Why B is wrong: Adam Smith gave the idea of absolute advantage (and the 'invisible hand').
Why C is wrong: Hicks contributed to general-equilibrium and welfare economics.
Note: Comparative advantage shows that countries gain from trade even if one is less efficient at producing everything.

Set 10 | Q.No 27 | Topic: Geography | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Which of the following plate boundaries formed the Himalayas?
   A) Divergent boundary
   B) Transform boundary
   C) Hotspot boundary
   D) Convergent boundary  <-- CORRECT
Answer: D
Why correct: The Himalayas were formed at a convergent plate boundary, where the Indian Plate collided with and pushed under the Eurasian Plate.
Why A is wrong: At a divergent boundary plates move apart, forming rifts and mid-ocean ridges.
Why B is wrong: At a transform boundary plates slide past each other (e.g. the San Andreas Fault).
Why C is wrong: A hotspot creates volcanic chains (like Hawaii), not fold mountains like the Himalayas.
Note: The Indian Plate is still pushing north, so the Himalayas continue to rise by a few millimetres each year.

Set 10 | Q.No 28 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Why are the days on Venus longer than its years?
   A) Venus has a slower rotation than revolution  <-- CORRECT
   B) Venus revolves very slowly around the Sun
   C) Venus does not rotate
   D) Venus spins on its axis in the opposite direction
Answer: A
Why correct: A day on Venus is longer than its year because Venus rotates on its axis very slowly - its single rotation (day) takes longer than one revolution around the Sun (year).
Why B is wrong: Venus actually revolves around the Sun faster than it spins, which is why the year is shorter.
Why C is wrong: Venus does rotate, just extremely slowly.
Why D is wrong: Venus does spin in the opposite (retrograde) direction, but the day-longer-than-year fact is due to its slow rotation.
Note: One Venus day equals about 243 Earth days, while a Venus year is about 225 Earth days.

   D) Jama Masjid
Answer: C
Why correct: The Nagina Masjid inside the Agra Fort was built by Shah Jahan for the ladies of the royal household and has three domes.
Why A is wrong: The Moti Masjid in Agra Fort is a larger pearl mosque, not the private ladies' mosque described.
Why B is wrong: The Mina Masjid was a tiny private mosque, not the three-domed ladies' mosque.
Why D is wrong: The Jama Masjid at Agra stands outside the fort and was built for the public.
Note: Shah Jahan, who built the Taj Mahal, was a great Mughal patron of marble architecture.

Set 10 | Q.No 30 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Which planet has a magnetic field that is offset from its center and tilted about 59 degrees to its rotational axis?
   A) Earth
   B) Jupiter
   C) Uranus  <-- CORRECT
   D) Saturn
Answer: C
Why correct: Uranus has a magnetic field that is offset from the planet's centre and tilted by about 59 degrees to its rotational axis - highly unusual among the planets.
Why A is wrong: Earth's magnetic field is only slightly tilted (about 11 degrees) and roughly centred.
Why B is wrong: Jupiter's field is strong but not tilted by ~59 degrees in this offset way.
Why D is wrong: Saturn's magnetic axis is almost aligned with its rotation axis.
Note: Uranus's strange tilted, off-centre magnetic field may be generated in its icy mantle rather than a metallic core.

Set 10 | Q.No 33 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Blood is classified under which type of animal tissue?
   A) Muscular tissue
   B) Nervous tissue
   C) Connective tissue  <-- CORRECT
   D) Epithelial tissue
Answer: C
Why correct: Blood is classified as connective tissue because its cells are suspended in a fluid matrix (plasma) and it connects and transports materials throughout the body.
Why A is wrong: Muscular tissue is contractile, unlike blood.
Why B is wrong: Nervous tissue conducts impulses; blood does not.
Why D is wrong: Epithelial tissue forms linings; blood is a fluid connective tissue.
Note: Plasma is the liquid matrix of blood, carrying red cells, white cells and platelets.

Set 10 | Q.No 34 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: English
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: Which of the following is an example of chemotropism in plants?
   A) Shoot bending towards light
   B) Root growing downwards
   C) Pollen tube growing towards ovule  <-- CORRECT
   D) Leaf folding on touch
Answer: C
Why correct: A pollen tube growing towards the ovule (in response to chemical signals from the ovary) is an example of chemotropism - growth directed by a chemical stimulus.
Why A is wrong: A shoot bending towards light is phototropism.
Why B is wrong: A root growing downwards is geotropism (gravitropism).
Why D is wrong: A leaf folding on touch (as in Mimosa) is thigmonasty/seismonasty, not chemotropism.
Note: Tropic movements are directional growth responses to stimuli such as light, gravity, water or chemicals.

Why C is wrong: It was not about wildlife trafficking.
Why D is wrong: It was not a river-pollution movement.
Note: The Chipko Movement began in the 1970s in the Garhwal Himalayas; Sunderlal Bahuguna was a key leader.

Set 11 | Q.No 24 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: Hindi
------------------------------------------------------------------------------
Q: न्यूटन के पहले नियम के अनुसार, कोई वस्तु तब तक स्थिर या एकसमान गति में रहती है जब तक
   A) इस पर बैलेंस्ड फोर्स काम करते हैं।
   B) गुरुत्वाकर्षण इसकी गति बदलता है।
   C) लगाया गया बल बदलाव के लिए मजबूर करता है।  <-- CORRECT
   D) घर्षण दूर हो जाता है।
Answer: C
Why correct: By Newton's first law (law of inertia), a body stays at rest or in uniform motion unless an applied (net external) force compels it to change its state.
Why A is wrong: Under balanced forces the body simply continues its state; it is an unbalanced force that changes motion.
Why B is wrong: Gravity is just one possible force; the law is about any net force.
Why D is wrong: Removing friction does not by itself cause change; a net applied force does.
Note: Newton's first law defines inertia - the tendency of a body to resist changes in its motion.

Why correct: Rani Lakshmibai was strongly supported by Tatya Tope, who fought alongside her against the British at Jhansi and Gwalior in 1857-58.
Why A is wrong: Rani Avantibai Lodhi led a separate revolt in Ramgarh.
Why B is wrong: Bahadur Shah Zafar was the symbolic leader at Delhi.
Why C is wrong: Begum Hazrat Mahal led the revolt at Lucknow.
Note: Tatya Tope was captured and executed in 1859; Rani Lakshmibai died fighting near Gwalior in 1858.

   C) अनुच्छेद 368  <-- CORRECT

Q: किसी विद्यार्थी को बारिश के ठीक बाद इंद्रधनुष दिखाई देता है। यदि वह इंद्रधनुष के निकट जाने की कोशिश करे, तो क्या होगा?
   A) वह इंद्रधनुष तक पहुंच जाएगा
   B) इंद्रधनुष अदृश्य हो जाएगा
   C) इंद्रधनुष समान दूरी पर दिखाई देगा  <-- CORRECT
   D) इंद्रधनुष रंग बदलेगा
Answer: C
Why correct: A rainbow is an optical effect formed at a fixed angle relative to the observer; as the student moves towards it, it appears to stay at the same distance and can never be reached.
Why A is wrong: One cannot actually reach a rainbow.
Why B is wrong: The rainbow does not vanish simply because one moves towards it.
Why D is wrong: The colours do not change as one approaches.
Note: A rainbow forms because raindrops refract, internally reflect and disperse sunlight at about a 42-degree angle.

Set 12 | Q.No 30 | Topic: Science & Technology | Language: Hindi

   A) सूर्य ग्रहण
   B) चंद्र ग्रहण  <-- CORRECT
   C) उल्का वृष्टि
   D) उत्तर ध्रुवीय ज्योति
Answer: B
Why correct: A lunar eclipse occurs when the Earth comes between the Sun and the Moon, blocking sunlight from reaching the Moon and casting Earth's shadow on it.

Why D is wrong: The aurora (northern lights) is caused by solar particles in the atmosphere.
Note: A lunar eclipse can occur only on a full-moon night when Sun, Earth and Moon are aligned.

   A) वायु की गुणवत्ता संवेदनशील समूहों के स्वास्थ्य पर प्रतिकूल प्रभाव डाल सकती है  <-- CORRECT
   B) वायु की गुणवत्ता उत्कृष्ट है
   C) वायु की गुणवत्ता संतोषजनक है
   D) वायु की गुणवत्ता सभी के लिए खतरनाक है
Answer: A
Why correct: In the Air Quality Index, the 'Moderate' category indicates that air quality may adversely affect the health of sensitive groups (such as people with respiratory issues).
Why B is wrong: 'Good' (not Moderate) means excellent air quality.
